      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n40633-2" target="نَهَرٌ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n40634"/></foreign> is also used in a pl. sense: as in the Kur, [liv. 54], <foreign lang="ar">فِى جَنَّاتٍ وَنَهَرٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">In gardens and</hi> among <hi rend="ital">rivers</hi>], i. e., <foreign lang="ar">أَنْهَارِ</foreign>; like the phrase in the Kur, (same chap. verse 45,] <foreign lang="ar">وَيُوَلُّونَ الدُّبْرَ</foreign>, (Fr, S.) meaning <foreign lang="ar">الأَدْبَارَ</foreign>, (Fr, TA:) but it is otherwise explained.                   <hi rend="ital">Much,</hi> (TA;) as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n40635-1" target="نَهيرٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>; (K, TA;) both applied to water. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  A <hi rend="ital">wide</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">نَهْر</foreign> [or river, or channel in which water runs]. (K.)       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">رَخُلٌ نَهِرٌ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">A man of day-time</hi>; syn. <foreign lang="ar">صَاحِبُ نَهَارٍ</foreign>; (S, K;) <hi rend="ital">who makes inroads or incursions into the territories of enemies therein:</hi> (S:) or <hi rend="ital">who works therein:</hi> (A:) a kind of rel. n.; as is shown by the ex. <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">لَسْتُ بِلَيْلِىٍّ وَلٰكِنِّى نهِرٌ</foreign>

                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">نَهَارٌ</orth>

                  <hi rend="ital">Day;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">day-time; contr. of</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">لَيْلٌ</foreign>: (S, TA:) or <hi rend="ital">broad daylight,</hi> (Mgh,) <hi rend="ital">from sunrise to sunset:</hi> (Mgh, Msb, K:) this is the original signification: (TA;) or this is the signification in the vulgar conventional language: but in the classical language it signifies the <hi rend="ital">time from the rising of the dawn to sunset:</hi> (Msb:) or the <hi rend="ital">light between the rising of the dawn and sunset:</hi> (K:) and so accord. to the lawyers: (TA:) in the trads., it is the whiteness of the <foreign lang="ar">نهار</foreign>, and the blackness of the <foreign lang="ar">ليل</foreign>; and there is nothing intervening between the <foreign lang="ar">ليل</foreign> and the <foreign lang="ar">نهار</foreign>: but sometimes the Arabs amplified, and applied <foreign lang="ar">نهار</foreign> to the <hi rend="ital">time from the clear shining of the dawn to the setting</hi> [<hi rend="ital">of the sun</hi>]: (Msb.) or (so accord. to the TA. but in some copies of the K, and the <hi rend="ital">spreading of the light</hi> [<hi rend="ital">which is a cause</hi>] <hi rend="ital">of sight</hi> and <hi rend="ital">its dispersion:</hi> (K:) in this explanation in the L, in the place of <foreign lang="ar">وَٱفْتِرَاقُهُ</foreign> we find <foreign lang="ar">وَٱجْتِمَاعُهُ</foreign> [and <hi rend="ital">its collecting together</hi>]: (TA:) it is also syn. with <foreign lang="ar">يَوْمٌ</foreign>; and is so when used without restriction in the non-fundamental sciences of religion, (<foreign lang="ar">الفُرُوع</foreign>,) as in the phrases <foreign lang="ar">صُمْ نَهَارًا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">fast thou a day</hi>] and <foreign lang="ar">إِعْمَلْ نَهَارًا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">work thou a day</hi>]: and it may be so used, or in its proper classical sense, when prefixed to <foreign lang="ar">يَوْم</foreign>, governing the latter in the gen. case: (Msb:) it has no proper dual, (Mgh, Msb,) and no proper pl., (S, Mgh, Msb, K, (like <foreign lang="ar">عَذَابٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">سَرَابٌ</foreign>; (S, K;) the former of which, however, has a pl. assigned to it [by Zj and] in the K, namely, <foreign lang="ar">أَعْذِبَةٌ</foreign>; (MF;) [and respecting the latter see <foreign lang="ar">شَرَابٌ</foreign>, with <foreign lang="ar">ش</foreign>;] [for] <foreign lang="ar">نهار</foreign> is a name applied to <hi rend="ital">every</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">يَوْم</foreign> [or <hi rend="ital">day</hi>]; and <foreign lang="ar">لَيْلٌ</foreign>, to every <foreign lang="ar">لَيْلَة</foreign> [or night]: one does not say <foreign lang="ar">نَهَارٌ وَنَهَارَانِ</foreign>, nor <foreign lang="ar">لَيْلٌ وَلَيْلَانِ</foreign>: but the sing. of <foreign lang="ar">نهار</foreign> is <foreign lang="ar">يَوْمٌ</foreign> (TA.) and the dual, <foreign lang="ar">يَوْمَانِ</foreign>, (Msb, TA:) and the pl., <foreign lang="ar">أَيَّامٌ</foreign>. (Msb:) and the contr. of <foreign lang="ar">يوْمٌ</foreign> is <foreign lang="ar">لَيْلَةٌ</foreign>, so says Az, on the authority of AHeyth (TA:) or it has pls.: namely, <foreign lang="ar">أَنْهُرٌ</foreign>, (IAar, S, K,) a pl. of pauc., (S,) in some lexicons <foreign lang="ar">أَنْهِرَةٌ</foreign>, (TA,) also a pl. of pauc.,] and <foreign lang="ar">نُهُرٌ</foreign>, (S, Mgh, Msb, K,) a pl. of mult. (S) [See also <foreign lang="ar">نَهَرٌ</foreign>.] Ibn-Keysán cites the following ex., <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">لَوْلَا الثَّرِيدَان لَمُتْنَا بِالضُّمُرْ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">ثَرِيدُ لَيْلٍ وَثرِيدٌ بِالنَّهُرْ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">Were it not for the two thereeds</hi> (or <hi rend="ital">messes of crumbled bread moistened with broth</hi>), <hi rend="ital">we had died of leanness: the thereed of night, and thereed in the day-times</hi>].
